                               Acknowledgments
This report was prepared by a World Bank team based on a study undertaken by the
consortium of Systema Transport Planning & Engineering Consultants Ltd and WYG with
financing from the Western Balkans Investment Framework (WBIF). The Directorate
General for Mobility and Transport (DG Move) of the European Commission (EC)
provided overall direction.

The World Bank (WB) core team was led by Baher El-Hifnawi and consisted of Liljana
Sekerinska, Evgenia Epaneshnikova and Nargis Ryskulova. The extended team included
Artan Guxho, Desa Stanić, Dragana Varezić, Elda Hafizi, Emre Eser, Ivana Bojić, Luan
Aliu, Jean-Francois Marteau, Alexandar Rowland and Senad Sačić. The Systema/Wyg
team was led by Dimitrios Tsamboulas and Athanasios Ballis and included Maja Popovic,
Michael Thomas, Lauri Ojala, George Emmanoulopoulos, Keith Cook, Yanni
Papapanagiotou and Natalia Tselenti. The study benefitted from comments from the Peer
Reviewers: Ana Simecki (DG NEAR, EC), Benedictus Eijbergen, Doerte Doemeland,
Olivier Le Ber and Shomik Mehndiratta; and Raymond Bourdeaux (World Bank). World
Bank Management: Juan Gaviria, Ellen Goldstein and Andras Horvai provided guidance
and comments on the successive report versions.

The team would like to express its appreciation to the SEETO Steering Committee and its
Secretariat for many discussions and comments provided during the course of the study.
The team would particularly like to thank the Secretariat for the coordination role it played
with the Regional Participants and for providing access to data and information, without
which the study would not have been possible. Thanks are also due to the many government
officials from the SEETO Regional Participants and Croatia who took the time to attend
progress review meetings and comment on the different reports and versions.

The Bank team is grateful for the guidance received from Alain Baron and Florian
Achleitner of the EC’s DG Move as well as from other EU Directorates and EU
Delegations to SEETO Regional Participants.

The Bank team would also like to thank the team for the EU-financed study: Accessibility
improved at border crossings for the integration of South East Europe (ACROSSEE) for
fruitful discussions and for sharing data and results from the study.

                               ANNEX I: 2030 REBIS Growth Rates




Annex I: 2030 Growth Factors
                                1
Introduction: Estimation of Growth Rates
1.     A transport planning model was developed to forecast transport flows from/to SEETO
Regional Participants and Croatia for year 2030.

2.       Socio-economic data for the base and future years is used to forecast transport flows in a
specific area. In this model, the socioeconomic variables included gross domestic product (GDP),
population size and number of jobs. With regard to estimating the base year freight flows, historical
data, provided by several sources such as EUROSTAT, International Monetary Fund (IMF), World
Bank, is used. Concerning projections for the future year of 2030, projections for the variables
mentioned above are developed. The data used and the process followed for the projection of GDP,
Population and Jobs for years 2030 are described below.

GDP

3.       The GDP of each zone is considered a major factor affecting transport flows. GDP
projections for 2014, 2015 and 2019 are based on the IMF’s 2014 World Economic Outlook.
Projections from 2020 to 2030 were developed by the study team in consultation with the World
Bank team taking into account current and recent economic conditions in the region and the growth
prospects given the stages of economic development of the different countries. Higher growth rates
were used to reflect higher intensity of economic activities in zones (e.g. capitals, ports, industrial
areas, etc.).

4.      The economic growth rates of the past few years were taken into account and adjusted
upwards to reflect the negative rates in some countries/Regional Participants at the present time.
These were adjusted to reflect a long-term sustainable growth rate given the stage of the economic
development. GDP growth rates were estimated for two scenarios: low/moderate and
moderate/high growth. Table AI.1 below presents the annual growth rate projections for each of
the Regional Participants/countries.

5.      The estimated growth rates have been used for the estimation of GDP of the zones included
in the model.

6.      For the zones that belong to one or more countries, the GDP growth rate was set equal to
the average of GDP growth rates of the countries included.

7.      The GDP growth rate of inner zones, which are part of one Regional Participant, was
estimated based on GDP growth rate of the country with following adjustments made. More
specifically, the GDP growth rate has been adjusted upwards for the following types of areas/
zones:

            o    Capitals of countries/ major cities
            o    Port areas/ ports
            o    Touristic areas
            o    Industrial areas (determined based on the development plans of the examined
                 countries where available).

Annex I: 2030 Growth Factors
                                                  2
8.     Finally, the growth rate of the remaining areas has been adjusted downwards to maintain
the same average growth rate of each country as initially estimated.

9.       The adjustment of the growth rate has been refined based on experts’ input in order to
reflect the expected growth in the different areas.

                   Table AI. 1. GDP Growth Rates per Country/Regional Participant (percentage)

                                                                                 Annual Average (2020-2030)
                                 2012    2013       2014         2015    2019       Low/       Moderate/
                                                                                 Moderate         High

    Bosnia and

       http://www.imf.org/external/pubs/ft/weo/2014/02/
      Annual average projections for the period 2020-2030 are based on study team’s assessment and consultation
       with the World Bank team.

Population

10.     Population projections for each of the regional percipients/countries were obtained from
the World Bank’s population datasets. 1 The estimated growth rates have been used for the
estimation of population of the zones included in the model.

11.     Concerning the zones including one or more countries, the growth rate of population has
been set equal to the average of the particular growth rates of the countries included.

12.    Population growth rate of inner zones, which are part of one country, was estimated based
on population growth rate of the country with following adjustments made. More specifically, the
GDP growth rate has been adjusted upwards for the following types of areas/ zones:
            o Capitals of countries/ major cities
            o Touristic areas


1
 The World Bank. (2013) Population Estimates and Projections. Available from:
http://datatopics.worldbank.org/hnp/popestimates

Annex I: 2030 Growth Factors
                                                             3
            o   Selected port areas (based on their specific characteristics)

13.      As in the GDP analysis, the adjustment of the growth rate has been refined based on
experts’ input in order to reflect the expected growth in the specific areas. Finally, the growth rate
of the remaining areas has been adjusted downwards to maintain the same average growth rate of
each country as initially estimated.

Employment

14.     The third socio-economic variable used in the model is called “JOBS”, representing the
employment in the examined areas. There are no datasets for future projections of employment.
Therefore, employment growth rates were estimated based on accepted empirical relationships
between economic growth and employment growth (employment intensity). The growth rate of
the employment in the examined areas for year 2030 has been estimated according to the estimates
of employment intensity for Europe and OKUN’s empirical formula (OKUN’s law: an empirically
observed relationship between unemployment and economic growth in each country). More
specifically, a two percent increase or decrease of GDP was projected to lead to a one percent
increase or decrease of employment in the examined areas. Based on this assumption, the
accumulated growth rate of the employment has been estimated, based on the accumulated GDP
growth rate, estimated for each zone, and using the formula mentioned above.

15.     However, considering that the formula would not always represent the existing situation
appropriately and in order to avoid an overestimation, an upper limit of the estimated employment
was determined. This was based on the principle that “the full employment could not exceed the
60 percent of total population”. As a result, in cases that the estimated employment of a zone
exceeded the 60 percent of population, the variable was set equal to 60 percent of the zone’s
population.

16.     The 2030 traffic projections for IWW and seaport were estimated using existing
(2012) traffic volumes and estimated growth factors for IWW transport and maritime ports.
For IWW only national data for each Regional Participant was used as a model input. Thus,
the estimation of traffic projections for the IWW sections is based on a single growth factor
for each Regional Participant, rather than a different growth factor for each port. These
growth factors were estimated based on GDP and population projections.

                                Table AI 3. Growth Factors for IWW Transport

                             Low/Moderate Scenario                                         Moderate/High Scenario

              Avg      growth                   growth                                  growth                   growth

              rate   passenger Passenger        traffic       Freight     growth      passenger    Passenger     traffic    Freight

Source: The World Bank Team estimates (GDP and elasticities) and Consultant’s estimates (growth factors)


17.     For passenger traffic at maritime ports, different growth factors for each port were
used, depending on its characteristics. More specifically, the level of tourism was taken
into account, as well as the proximity to significant tourist attractions. To this end, for
example, the port of Dubrovnik was assumed to have higher growth factors due to the fact
that the city is a major touristic attraction and is expected to continue to be a major
destination for international passenger traffic. For the ports of Ploce and Rijeka, which both
have a strong freight orientation, lower growth factors for passenger traffic were assumed.
With regards to the port of Bar, which is the main Montenegro port, it is believed to have
a high potential to attract tourist flows with some capacity for cargo, while the port of
Durres in Albania is already serving a significant number of passengers.

                   ANNEX V: Capacity Considerations for the Road Network




Annex V: Capacity considerations for the road network
                                                  140
1.       For the purposes of the study, an assessment of road capacity for each road section was
made based on the “ideal” values for the “ideal” base conditions suitably downgraded due to
specific deficiencies such as sub-standard road widths, pavement deterioration, difficult
terrain/gradients and/or significant heavy vehicle (HGV) traffic, to produce “modified” tabulations
for road capacity as shown below.

Annex VI: Road section grouping by intervention
                                                     141
                            ANNEX VI: Road Section Grouping by Intervention




Annex VI: Road section grouping by intervention
                                                  142
1.        Four broad categories were used to define the interventions:

(i)     Road sections that require no immediate upgrading
There are a few complete corridors/highways that fall into that category:
 ROAD 9 - Croatia – all sections [Vukovar-Vinkovci-Zupanja]
 ROAD Xa - Croatia – all sections [Zagreb/Donji Macelj – Jankomir]
 ROAD Xb - Serbia – all sections [Horgos-Subotica-Novi Sad-Batajnica-Dobanovci]
In addition, there are many sections within each corridor which also fall into this category.
(ii)     Road sections that are candidates for immediate rehabilitation to preserve capacity
These are road sections where existing pavement conditions are in need of rehabilitation; otherwise,
they will suffer a consequent reduced road capacity caused by these existing conditions. Road
maintenance and rehabilitation works mainly aim at addressing deteriorating pavement conditions.
(iii)    Road sections that are candidates for immediate upgrading (upgrading works or
         widening) to increase capacity
These are specific sections where the current road conditions require immediate
upgrading/widening works to increase capacity to meet the current traffic projections. Some of
these road sections require widening from 2 lanes to 4 lanes (in some cases from 4 lanes to 6 lanes),
whereas there are other road sections that only require alternative lower cost upgrading works such
as provision of crawling lanes, road shoulders, improved lane widths, improved geometry, junction
improvements, etc.
(iv)     Road sections that are candidates for future upgrading (upgrading works or widening)
         to increase capacity in the future
These are specific sections where the current road conditions may require future
upgrading/widening works to increase capacity to meet the 2030 traffic projections. It is therefore
recommended that these specific sections should be subject to further studies in due course, in
preparation for works implementation at a later date, which may be in the range from 2020 onwards
up to 2030.
2.    In the following Table AVI.1, the proposed interventions for the existing road network are
summarized for both low/moderate and moderate/high economic growth scenario.

Annex VI: Road section grouping by intervention
                                                                                   151
ANNEX VII: Possible Interventions to Increase Capacity of the Railway
                                                             Network




Annex VII: Possible interventions for the railway network
                                                    152
1.       Possible interventions for railway sections with capacity constraints, in order to increase
their capacity, include the construction of a double track, line improvements (e.g. station, additional
sidings, ballast, curves improvement etc.), and block and signaling system upgrades. The proposed
possible interventions rely on expert experience and while appropriate for strategic assessment,
would require feasibility studies prior to making a decision to move forward. More specifically the
possible interventions are:

       Adding second track: The number of tracks has a major impact on capacity: two tracks
        usually have around four times more capacity than a single track. However, adding a
        second track may not eliminate the problem because stations could constitute a real
        bottleneck. Auxiliary tracks at crossing stations also increase the capacity of a single track
        because they allow trains to carry out crossings and overtaking.
        Managing Network effects: A single line cannot be considered as a fully independent
        part of the whole network due to crossing and overlapping lines, which can be true
        bottlenecks. As a consequence, the capacity of a line cannot be defined without considering
        what happens on the interfering lines.
       Track structure and speed limits: The condition of the rails, ties, and ballast dictate the
        weight and type of equipment that can be used on the line, as well as the speeds allowed
        on the line. They have an important influence on the capacity.
       Length of line sections: Lengths of line sections between stations (where crossing and
        overtaking are allowed) are important, mainly, on single track sections.
       Train mix: Railway capacity is dependent on the traffic mix. As the mixture of different
        train increases, more interference is generated. Thus, trains require overtaking and
        crossings, and the mixture reduces the traffic flow.
       Manage Traffic peaking factor: The concentration of traffic within a short time period
        has significant impact on capacity. Effort should be done to spread the peaks.
       Manage Train heterogeneity: The heterogeneity in double-track and single-track cases
        affects capacity. In single-track lines, capacity is more affected by train speed than by
        heterogeneity. In double-track lines, the capacity is affected by heterogeneity more than
        by train speed.
        Implement modern signaling, ERTMS: To ensure the safe operations and enable
        optimization of the line capacity, the specifications of ERTMS include the calculation
        method of the headway time between consecutive trains.

The International Sava River Basin Commission works towards a plan for the rehabilitation and improvement of the Sava River waterway through dredging and construction of sills (to increase the
water level), construction of groynes (to achieve higher flow velocities) and other works that would upgrade navigation to class IV. Such improvement will allow river ports on the Sava river (Slavonski
Brod and Sisak) to exploit their current capacities, attract induced traffic and probably justify future plans.

The master plan of Slavonski Brod foresees bio-diesel plan, wood processing, cement storage etc. Sisak port perspective is less demanding as the unfavorable port location in the Kupa river and the
bridges between the Kupa-Sava confluence, pose barriers to future development.

Source: SEETO (2012), Consultant’s estimates (2030 projections and capacity considerations)

The International Sava River Basin Commission works towards a plan for the rehabilitation and improvement of the Sava River waterway through dredging and construction of sills (to increase
the water level), construction of groynes (to achieve higher flow velocities) and other works that would upgrade navigation to class IV. Such improvement will allow river ports on the Sava river
(Brcko and Samac) to exploit their current capacities, attract induced traffic and probably justify future plans.
Brcko port requires equipment investments to continue to improve both its capacity and operational efficiency. After the implementation of these long-term investments, the maximum capacity is
estimated at 720,000 tons. Samac port have started an ambitious investment plan for rehabilitation aiming at infrastructure improvements, installation of modern cargo handling equipment, and
establishment of storage facilities.


Source: SEETO (2012), Consultant’s estimates (2030 projections and capacity considerations)

             ANNEX IX: Assessment of the 2003 REBIS Traffic Projections




Annex IX: Assessment of the 2003 REBIS Traffic Projections
                                                169
1.      The 2012 traffic projections for the main links of the SEETO Comprehensive
Network from the 2003 REBIS study were reviewed and assessed against reported traffic
counts (as per SEETO database and traffic counts undertaken by the Consultant) in order
to assess the accuracy of the projections. The main goal of this analysis was to identify
possible gaps in the assumptions, which would be used to inform model development for
the update.

2.     The review showed significant variations which were not consistent across the
network or at the national level. The forecasted traffic on some sections of the network was
underestimated by the REBIS 2003 study. More specifically, reported AADT is more than
100% of the respective REBIS 2003 study forecasts on:

     22% of the road links in Albania
     16% of the road links in Bosnia and Herzegovina
     42% of the road links in the former Yugoslav Republic of Macedonia
     16% of the road links in Serbia
     53% of the road links in Croatia
     20% of the road links in Montenegro
     75% of the road network in Kosovo*
     32% of the SEETO Comprehensive Road Network

3.         The detailed results are presented below.

                                  2003 REBIS Moderate Scenario - Albania
                                               Forecast 2006     Forecast 2015     Forecast 2025

    General results for Albania
    Population (in millions)                        3.62             3.89              4.21
    Index income per capita 2001 prices             130              214                371
    Level of car ownership (cars/1.000              51               113                232
    inhabitants)
    Traffic growth rates                         2001-2006        2001-2015          2001-2025
    Passenger cars                                  63%             299%               850%
    Trucks - national                               46%             186%               507%
    Trucks - international                          25%              87%               194%
    Rail freight C                                  17%              56%               115%
    Rail passengers                                 20%              65%               136%


    Passenger Cars                              2012 forecast   ADT cars 2012    ADT /forecast R
                                                2003 REBIS        -SEETO
    Hani I Hoti - Shkoder                           8433            3750             44.5%
    Shkoder - Lezhe                                 3939            6426             163.1%
    Lezhe - Fushe Kruje                             5834            10946            187.6%
Annex IX: Assessment of the 2003 REBIS Traffic Projections
                                                170
 Fushe Kruje - Vore                              7727            7456             96.5%
